**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Now, Elon Musk is leaving his role as the head of DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

Elections, political figures, and government actions

# DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025

## TRUMP ADMINISTRATION & EXECUTIVE ACTIONS

### Presidential Approval & Public Opinion

President Trump's approval rating has stagnated or declined across multiple polls. A Reuters/Ipsos poll shows Trump's overall approval holding steady at 42%, though his support on immigration policy has weakened [1]. Other polls paint a more concerning picture, with Newsweek reporting Trump's "worst polls yet" with descriptions like "awful, awful, awful" [2]. The trend appears to cross partisan lines, with another report indicating Trump's approval rating has "plunged" even with a Republican pollster [3].

[1] Trump approval steady at 42%, support weakens for his immigration policy, Reuters/Ipsos poll finds, https://www.reuters.com/world/us/trump-approval-steady-42-support-weakens-his-immigration-policy-reutersipsos-2025-06-16/

  
[2] Donald Trump Approval Rating Suffers Worst Polls Yet—'Awful, Awful, Awful', https://www.newsweek.com/donald-trump-approval-rating-worst-polls-2086089

  
[3] Donald Trump's approval rating plunges with Republican pollster, https://www.newsweek.com/donald-trump-approval-rating-polls-2086533

### Executive Departments & Agency Actions

The Trump administration has disbanded a group focused on pressuring Russia, according to Reuters [1]. Domestically, cuts to FEMA's storm preparation program are disproportionately affecting communities that supported Trump in previous elections [2].

[1] Trump administration disbands group focused on pressuring Russia, sources say, https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/trump-administration-disbands-group-focused-pressuring-russia-sources-say-2025-06-17/?utm_source=reddit.com

  
[2] Cuts to FEMA's storm prep program hammer communities that voted for Trump, https://www.cbsnews.com/femagrantcuts/

### Presidential Communications & Business Interests

President Trump's recent communications have been confrontational across multiple fronts. Following shootings of Minnesota lawmakers, Trump declined to call Governor Walz, stating it would "waste time" [1]. His administration's cuts to federal grants have prompted researchers to warn of an impending "brain drain" [2]. After leaving the G7 summit early, Trump blasted an unnamed "publicity seeking" world leader [3].

On the business front, Trump has secured a "golden share" in U.S. Steel, granting him "extraordinary control" over the company [4]. The Trump Organization has launched "Trump Mobile," featuring a $499 smartphone [5]. Despite marketing claims, the "all-American" smartphone is actually manufactured in China [6].

[1] Trump says he won't call Minnesota Gov. Walz after lawmaker shootings because it would 'waste time', https://apnews.com/article/trump-walz-minnesota-lawmakers-shot-call-064092d14bea4c3141da31b7a5e5c9b3

## FOREIGN POLICY & INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

### Israel-Iran Conflict & Middle East Crisis

The Israel-Iran conflict has reached a critical juncture, with President Trump facing intense pressure regarding U.S. involvement. The Pentagon has signaled the U.S. won't strike Iran directly, even as Trump has summoned the Security Council [1]. Israel is seeking more U.S. assistance to target Iran's nuclear program [2], with Israeli Defense Minister Gallant stating the U.S. "has an obligation" to assist Israel's operation [3].

Trump has publicly stated he wants a "real end" to the nuclear problem with Iran [4] and reportedly urged evacuation of Tehran before leaving the G7 summit early [5]. Conflicting assessments have emerged about Iran's nuclear capabilities, with Israel claiming Iran was racing toward a nuclear weapon while U.S. intelligence indicated it was years away [6]. The situation represents a significant test for Trump, who reportedly shifted from opposing Israel's strikes on Iran to reluctant support [7].

President Trump's early departure from the G7 summit created diplomatic tensions. ### Healthcare & Medicaid

Republican proposals to cut Medicaid by approximately $800 billion are advancing despite the program's growing popularity [1]. A study reported by STAT News indicates the cuts could result in more than 16,000 preventable deaths annually [2]. The cuts have triggered political fallout for some Republicans, including Senator Joni Ernst, whose response that "we all are going to die" has apparently damaged her reelection prospects [3].

[1] Medicaid keeps getting more popular as Republicans aim to cut it by $800 billion, https://www.npr.org/sections/shots-health-news/2025/06/17/nx-s1-5435312/medicaid-cuts-big-beautiful-bill-trump-kff-poll

### Regulatory Policy & Financial Reform

The Environmental Protection Agency is reconsidering a ban on cancer-causing asbestos [1]. In a separate regulatory development, Kraft Heinz will remove all artificial dyes from its food products in compliance with demands from Health and Human Services Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. [2].

Financial regulatory changes have sparked controversy across multiple fronts. The Senate is poised to pass cryptocurrency legislation without addressing Trump's own investments in the sector [3], while observers have expressed shock at what's described as "open corruption" regarding Trump's crypto deals and loosening of regulations [4]. Questions have emerged about the Department of Government Efficiency's (DOGE) involvement with Social Security, with Vanity Fair reporting that "Musk's team simply did not understand the data" [5].

## IMMIGRATION & BORDER SECURITY

### ICE Operations & Policy Impact

Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) operations have intensified following policy changes. Officials have reversed guidance that previously exempted farms and hotels from immigration raids [1], leading to increased enforcement activity. The human impact of these operations is highlighted in several reports: an Army sergeant's wife was deported despite the family believing they were safe [2], Cuban-Americans in Miami are expressing concerns about deportations [3], and a study found immigration raids in Central California led to increased student absences for months [4].

The Trump administration's immigration goals are creating fiscal challenges for ICE, according to The New Republic, which characterizes the objectives as "bonkers" and claims they are "driving ICE bankrupt" [5].

The human impact of these operations is highlighted in several reports: an Army sergeant's wife was deported despite the family believing they were safe [2], Cuban-Americans in Miami are expressing concerns about deportations [3], and a study found immigration raids in Central California led to increased student absences for months [4].

The Trump administration's immigration goals are creating fiscal challenges for ICE, according to The New Republic, which characterizes the objectives as "bonkers" and claims they are "driving ICE bankrupt" [5].

[1] Trump officials reverse guidance exempting farms, hotels from immigration raids, https://www.washingtonpost.com/immigration/2025/06/16/trump-farms-hotels-immigration-raids/?utm_campaign=wp_main&utm_medium=social&utm_source=reddit.com  
  
[2] "They're taking Shirly": An Army sergeant thought his family as safe. Then ICE deported his wife., https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2025/06/army-sergeant-thought-his-family-was-safe-then-ice-deported-his-wife-shirly-guardado/  
  
[3] In Miami, deportations are raising concerns among Cuban-Americans, https://www.npr.org/2025/06/11/nx-s1-5428118/in-miami-deportations-are-raising-concerns-among-cuban-americans  
  
[4] Immigration Raids in Central California Increased Student Absences for Months: Study, https://www.hoover.org/news/immigration-raids-central-california-increased-student-absences-months-study  
  
[5] Trump's Bonkers Immigration Goals Are Driving ICE Bankrupt, https://newrepublic.com/post/196869/donald-trump-immigration-goals-ice-broke-money
